  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e61cf668-7c71-45ee-968b-7db32b89e0a3'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText15955745068552483066" style="display:none">Of all the folks in the mountain shacks, the Casteels were the lowest -- the scum of the hills. <br /> Heaven Leigh Casteel was the prettiest, smartest girl in the backwoods, despite her ragged clothes and dirty face...despite a father meaner than ten vipers...despite her weary stepmother, who worked her like a mule. For her brother Tom and the little ones, Heaven clung to her pride and her hopes. Someday they'd get away and show the world that they were decent, fine and talented -- worthy of love and respect. <br /> Then Heaven's stepmother ran off, and her wicked, greedy father had a scheme -- a vicious scheme that threatened to destroy the precious dream of Heaven and the children forever!</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4490376-sarah-mac?shelf=soggy-beta-boner">soggy-beta-boner</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4490376-sarah-mac?shelf=cover-me-black">cover-me-black</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4490376-sarah-mac?shelf=cover-me-teal">cover-me-teal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4490376-sarah-mac?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4490376-sarah-mac?shelf=vc-universe">vc-universe</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer234481657" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3887453754013472815">Here's another book that screws with the grading curve. If you look at other 4-star reads -- <i>Frankenstein</i>, for example -- there's no way poor VC Andrews can measure up. Yet my verdict stands...four shiny stars, the sign of a book I plan to keep around, & I'm not ashamed to admit it. (Don't look, Mary Shelley.)<br/><br/>This book is loosely divided into three sections. The first is Heaven's life in the West Virginia mountains. As the blurb indicates, her Casteel family is hillbilly scum -- poor, dirty, & p</span>
  <span id="freeText3887453754013472815" style="display:none">Here's another book that screws with the grading curve. If you look at other 4-star reads -- <i>Frankenstein</i>, for example -- there's no way poor VC Andrews can measure up. Yet my verdict stands...four shiny stars, the sign of a book I plan to keep around, &amp; I'm not ashamed to admit it. (Don't look, Mary Shelley.)<br /><br />This book is loosely divided into three sections. The first is Heaven's life in the West Virginia mountains. As the blurb indicates, her Casteel family is hillbilly scum -- poor, dirty, &amp; proud enough to ignore the discomforts of both. Abandoned by their stepmother &amp; ignored by their asshole father (Luke), teenage Heaven &amp; her brother Tom struggle to provide for their three younger siblings &amp; near-crippled grandfather. I enjoyed this section quite a bit -- a sort of <i>Special Victims Unit</i> meets <i>Boxcar Children</i> mashup of melodrama. Of course, this being VCA, you know things will soon take a turn for the crazeh. That crazeh comes when their worthless father decides to sell his kids for $500 each. Blinded by rage &amp; ignorance, Heaven chooses to escape with a yuppie couple...and so begins the second section, her new life with Kitty &amp; Cal.<br /><br />Kitty is another refugee from the hillbilly mountains, &amp; she plans to train Heaven as a housekeeper/revenge trophy against Luke, who knocked her up when she was Heaven's age. Kitty is an abusive, shrill cougar; not content to vent her issues on the world at large, she's also OCD, demanding fresh linens every day, color-coded towels, etc. All this wouldn't be so bad except she delights in abusing Heaven at every opportunity -- verbally, physically, or mentally, whichever is most convenient. But for all her flaws, Kitty is somewhat sympathetic. She really <i>doesn't</i> know how to love someone properly; she really <i>does</i> think she's doing Heaven a service by dragging her from the mountainside &amp; plopping her into daughterly servitude. In Kitty's eyes, anything is better than being a hill-scum whore.<br /><br />It's a twisted, if understandable, point of view...as opposed to Cal, her milksop 20-something husband, who has the backbone of a wet noodle. He repeatedly threatens to leave Kitty because of the ways she abuses Heaven, but he never does. There's some twaddle about him being in debt to her for starting his business, but adult readers can see it's much simpler than that -- i.e., sex. *snort* Of course it's not long before this affection-starved noodle-boner turns his attention to Kitty's adopted daughter. Heaven, for her part, doesn't want sex with Cal. She knows it must be wrong...but she's so desperate for fatherly love that she allows him to seduce her with his wishy-washy emo ways. Cal's seduction is probably the most sinister aspect of the book; it's both creepy &amp; sad that Heaven is so inexperienced &amp; desperate for love that she allows that kind of affection. It's abuse that's veiled by the abuser &amp; victim both, which is equal parts disturbing &amp; fascinating. Nobody but an inexperienced farm-girl would allow that wimpy assface in their pants. Seriously, the guy is a definite flop in the romantic hero department.<br /><br /><br /><b>-SARAH'S SCALE OF HERO HOTNESS-<br /><br />[...Always Uber Hot...]</b><br /><br />Daryl Dixon <br />Bucky Barnes (<i>Captain America</i>)<br />misunderstood anti-heroes<br />bastard sons of villains<br />Peter Maximoff (<i>X-Men</i>)<br />understated badasses with tattoos<br />Boromir<br />.<br />.<br />Hicks (<i>Aliens</i>)<br /><i>The 13th Warrior</i> vikings<br />Rhett Butler<br />.<br />.<br />.<br /><br /><b>[...Frequently Hot...]</b><br /><br />assassins<br />heroes in waistcoats &amp; cravats <br />Tig Trager (<i>Sons of Anarchy</i>)<br />Jaime Lannister<br />.<br />.<br />self-righteous celibate warriors<br />Ethan Chandler (<i>Penny Dreadful</i>)<br />Spock (original <i>Trek</i>)<br />snarky alphas<br />.<br />.<br />.<br /><br /><b>[...Meh, No Thanks...]</b><br /><br />Heathcliffe (<i>Wuthering Heights</i>)<br />schmoopy Regency rakes<br />.<br />.<br />.<br /><br /><b>[...Not Hot...]</b><br /><br />Ebenezer Scrooge <br />.<br />.<br />.<br />Grima Wormtongue<br />.<br />.<br />.<br />.<br />.<br />Michael Meyers<br />Theon Greyjoy (<i>Game of Thrones</i>)<br />potato salad<br />potato salad with celery<br />.<br />.<br />.<br /><br /><b>[...Definitely Not Ever Hot...]</b><br /><br />Edward Cullen<br />Ramsey Bolton (<i>Game of Thrones</i>)<br />.<br />.<br />.<br />lizard people<br />.<br />.<br />Cal<br />.<br />.<br />Christian Grey<br />Bart (<i>Dollanganger</i> novels)<br />puppy-kickers<br /><br /><br />...There, see what I mean? <br /><br />Anyhow, the third part of the novel has juxtaposition of Kitty's obnoxious family vs Heaven trying to gather her siblings back together, but the climax is Heaven's resolve to find her mother's roots in Boston (not a spoiler, since something's gotta fill the next three books :P). That should prove rather interesting. It's VCA, after all...WTFery is always on the menu.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3887453754013472815" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Michelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54041-michelle"><img alt="Michelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316924020p2/54041.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/79702250?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle" href="/user/show/54041-michelle">Michelle</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer79702250" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13027150806241016026">Um...I almost gave this five stars because I love V.C. and her trashy, soap opera books (but, you know, it's not beautifully written or anything so I restrained myself). I must say: I am horrified by the amount of people that I've proudly told I'm reading V.C. again, only to receive a confused or blank look in return. Is V.C. Andrews not required reading for teenagers? And let me tell you, it still holds up for us adults. <br/><br/>It's been a looong time since I last read Heaven, and I was expecting all </span>
  <span id="freeText13027150806241016026" style="display:none">Um...I almost gave this five stars because I love V.C. and her trashy, soap opera books (but, you know, it's not beautifully written or anything so I restrained myself). I must say: I am horrified by the amount of people that I've proudly told I'm reading V.C. again, only to receive a confused or blank look in return. Is V.C. Andrews not required reading for teenagers? And let me tell you, it still holds up for us adults. <br /><br />It's been a looong time since I last read Heaven, and I was expecting all of these things in this book: (1) at least one dead parent, (2) a wealthy grandparent, (3) a boarding school, (4) a witch (why are you laughing? <a href="http://completevca.com/pics_casteel_heaven.shtml" rel="nofollow noopener">look at this cover</a>--that lady is crazy-looking), (5) an incestuous relationship with an uncle who doesn't know he's the girl's uncle until it's too late!, (6) somebody to sculpt or paint or be in a cranberry bog (I think those are in other series, maybe?), (7) an adoption, (8) and a bastard child.<br /><br />So not all of that happened, but it was still pretty darn exciting. And, actually, the writing isn't THAT horrible.<br /><br />DO NOT start reading the later series from V.C. because those really are horribly written--I think the ghostwriters weren't selected as well, and I think they stopped using V.C.'s actual plots and notes and just started slapping together books using all of the 8 elements I listed above (and probably more). Start out as you should with Flowers in the Attic and go through the series as they were published. I am adding this very helpful link for you sad people that have yet to experience the awesome trashiness that is V.C. Andrews: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.completevca.com/index.shtml">http://www.completevca.com/index.shtml</a><br /><br />Go forth, enjoy, and you're welcome.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13027150806241016026" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell"><img alt="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584062476p2/2190064.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=you-can-watch-it-on-the-telly">you-can-watch-it-on-the-telly</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=ya-ya-land">ya-ya-land</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=gothic">gothic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2913627624" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16627879552009487861"><a href='http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/> <br/>The Casteel series was the last of the family sagas that V.C. Andrews had a hand in before she died and her ghostwriter took over. It's impossible not to compare it to the <i>Dollanganger </i>series, especially since both approximate what you'd get if you decided to adapt a bodice-ripper for the not-so-discerning young-adult audience. On a scale of one to trash, this ranks a solid Bertrice Small: the writing is just as melodramatic, and Andrew</span>
  <span id="freeText16627879552009487861" style="display:none"><a href="http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br> <br>The Casteel series was the last of the family sagas that V.C. Andrews had a hand in before she died and her ghostwriter took over. It's impossible not to compare it to the <i>Dollanganger </i>series, especially since both approximate what you'd get if you decided to adapt a bodice-ripper for the not-so-discerning young-adult audience. On a scale of one to trash, this ranks a solid Bertrice Small: the writing is just as melodramatic, and Andrews regularly and predictably makes out parental figures to be abusive the same way that Small could be counted on to make all of her villains libertines and deviants.<br><br><br><br>HEAVEN is about a young girl named Heaven Leigh (get it?) Casteel. She lives in the hills, cramped in a small shed with her four other siblings, grandparents, father, and stepmother. She is the only child from her father's first marriage; her mother died in childbirth, and her father kept her on a pedestal in his mind. No other woman can match up, not even his daughters or his new wife, so he mostly ignores his children, abuses his wife, and is a regular attendee of the local "den of ill repute" despite the fact that they're all starving.<br><br><br><br>Heaven catches the eye of a rich boy because of her beauty, and this is a trope of Andrews's, too: there's always a soft and sensitive boy hero figure to whisk the heroine away from her wretched life-- until he proves to be just as disturbing as everyone else, only better at hiding it. Logan doesn't have a chance to show off any true colors he might have, though, as Heaven's father gets an STD, and kind of loses it after his wife has a deformed stillborn child; he gets the brilliant idea that the solution to their money problems is to sell off his children for $500/ea. to local rich people in the area.<br><br><br><br>Heaven gets sent off to live with a woman named Kitty, but her nickname could be "Mommie Dearest." She lives in a house filled with creepy ceramic animals and everything is pink. She has violent mood swings, and living in Casa de Crazy, you could find yourself having your hair lovingly combed out one minute, only to be thrown into a scalding hot Lysol bath the next (note: pretty sure this Lysol name-drop in the book was #notsponsored). Her only solace in this house is Kitty's young husband, Cal, but his feelings towards Heaven-- as you would expect-- aren't exactly pure.<br><br><br><br>HEAVEN was a good book-- and by a good book I mean it told a good story, even though the writing was arguably not good. It reminded me a lot of the stories I used to read on FictionPress back in the day, with its long laundry list of soap opera plot devices, and the fact that virtually every character in this book except for the good ones were villains. I hated Kitty, and I also hated Heaven's siblings, especially Fanny and "Our Jane." Tom was also creepy, and he and Heaven definitely had a "Flowers in the Attic" vibe going on, and I'm worried about what might happen with their relationship in the next book. Logan will be back, I'm sure, but whether he stays nice and heroic is anyone's guess.<br><br><br><br>If you're into bodice-rippers and vintage sleaze, I really can't urge you strongly enough to pick up V.C. Andrews's books. There is nothing quite like them, and you can take that how you like.<br><br><br><br>3 to 3.5 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="16627879552009487861" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3521990773" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3521990773" />
    <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt"><img alt="Rebecca McNutt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602390057p2/36977686.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3521990773?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca McNutt" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt">Rebecca McNutt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/55165704-heaven">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=gothic">gothic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3521990773" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8589426404448458547">I've often not been a big fan of V.C. Andrews books due to their incestuous subject matter, although the writing has always been poetically gothic and beautiful, and I admire Andrews herself as an author who's led such an interesting life. I'm unsure if this is actually one of her works, or her ghostwriter's, but <i>Heaven</i> in many ways mimics the eerily quaint, innocent writing style of Andrews' "Dollanganger" series, although its main character is a lot more human (I personally found) and easier t</span>
  <span id="freeText8589426404448458547" style="display:none">I've often not been a big fan of V.C. Andrews books due to their incestuous subject matter, although the writing has always been poetically gothic and beautiful, and I admire Andrews herself as an author who's led such an interesting life. I'm unsure if this is actually one of her works, or her ghostwriter's, but <i>Heaven</i> in many ways mimics the eerily quaint, innocent writing style of Andrews' "Dollanganger" series, although its main character is a lot more human (I personally found) and easier to relate to, and the setting stands out as much less polished and more realistic.<br /><br /><i>Heaven</i> does, once again, deal with disturbing subject matter: child abuse, family dysfunction, poverty and rampant greed, but through it all, main character Heaven's resilience as she struggles to protect herself and her siblings, living with her redneck father in the mountains, it makes for a very admirable character who does what she has to do to survive, although much of it is traumatic and upsetting. Heaven wants a better life, and like Cathy and Christopher of Andrews' <i>Flowers in the Attic</i>, she's determined to find it. <br /><br />While this book seems to in many ways copy the formula of <i>Flowers in the Attic</i> with its gothic abuse and cruel parent figures, <i>Heaven</i> is one I'd recommend for readers who weren't as charmed with the glamour and wealth of the "Dollanganger" series, who might be looking for a more down-to-earth scenario. The themes may bother some readers, and I also found them a bit off-putting, but the character development and vocabulary made up for it in spades.<br /><br />*As a side note, I love this hardcover edition from the 1980's, released in Britain with a cloud stencil and pretty coloured stars all over it. It really gives off a retro aesthetic.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8589426404448458547" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/563822831?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo Scott" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo Scott" href="/user/show/18461578-jo-scott">Jo Scott</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer563822831" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3765737390880398808">Her stories might seem sensational even trashy but at least V Andrews was talking about the ugly. This and Andrews other books, made my ugly feel less lonely, it kept me company at night, when my ugly was creeping outside my bedroom door demanding a sandwich from his cooperative wife before he moved on to complete his nights work.<br/> In an era when the misery memoir was not so present, before child-line and the wider acceptance of abuse in the home she unconsciously kept a lot of abuse victims comp</span>
  <span id="freeText3765737390880398808" style="display:none">Her stories might seem sensational even trashy but at least V Andrews was talking about the ugly. This and Andrews other books, made my ugly feel less lonely, it kept me company at night, when my ugly was creeping outside my bedroom door demanding a sandwich from his cooperative wife before he moved on to complete his nights work.<br /> In an era when the misery memoir was not so present, before child-line and the wider acceptance of abuse in the home she unconsciously kept a lot of abuse victims company when no one else wanted to know. Weird thing but when I started facing up to my past ugly I gave all her books away, now I want them back.<br />Now studying literature I am wondering about her place among writers. Is it really trashy? Or is it highlighting the long history of oppression and abuse of women. It plays on real fears , the book was written years ago but we still live in a world where it is still not as safe for a female to walk down the same street alone at night as it for a male. Heaven is a good character, there is something about her that makes her strong, appealing and memorable. As a witness to the ugly, with a family that belongs Jerry Springer show or a soap, I refuse to be ashamed for having V C Andrews entire collection in my literary past, and I thank her for being there.</span>

<div id="review_2911598919" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2911598919" />
    <a title="Bookiverse" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49511007-bookiverse"><img alt="Bookiverse" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548295706p2/49511007.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2911598919?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bookiverse" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bookiverse" href="/user/show/49511007-bookiverse">Bookiverse</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49511007-bookiverse?shelf=read-scary-level-5">read-scary-level-5</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2911598919" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7188052478989985854">I wanted to reread Heaven because the screen adaptation was scheduled to air last Saturday on Lifetime. So, I reread it and I want to tell you why this book is a MUST READ!<br/><br/>V.C. Andrews was one of my all time favorite authors until she died in 1986 and her family hired a ghostwriter, Andrew Neiderman, to finish some her WIPs. Decades later, in my opinion no one has written such genre-bending [Gothic/contemporary/suspense/thriller/mystery/horror], complex and dark, generational sagas filled with d</span>
  <span id="freeText7188052478989985854" style="display:none">I wanted to reread Heaven because the screen adaptation was scheduled to air last Saturday on Lifetime. So, I reread it and I want to tell you why this book is a MUST READ!<br /><br />V.C. Andrews was one of my all time favorite authors until she died in 1986 and her family hired a ghostwriter, Andrew Neiderman, to finish some her WIPs. Decades later, in my opinion no one has written such genre-bending [Gothic/contemporary/suspense/thriller/mystery/horror], complex and dark, generational sagas filled with dysfunctional families, ugly secrets and forbidden love like V.C. Andrews.<br /><br />Especially, I haven’t found anyone else that has written extreme poverty, adversities and hardships like her. The physical and emotional imagery is superb. You cannot only actually "see" the two-room shack in the hills of West Virginia too small for the family of nine, or hear and feel the howling wind filtering through the wood’s cracks, you can smell the shack, the dirty cloths and the fumes from the latrine because there is no running water or bathrooms, or smell the rotting food that you’ll have to eat if you don’t want to starve…. You can also really feel the pang of starvation in you stomach, the embarrassment of being “Of all the folks in the mountain shacks, the lowest, the scum of the hills”, the desperation of seeing your younger siblings starve to death, and the despair and fear of being hated, abused, neglected and ultimately abandoned by your parents.<br /><br />If you want to connect with characters at unexpected levels and desperately root for them, even for the evilest of them, because of everything they have been put through… If you want to wince, gasp, hold your breath, cry… all the feels… you gotta read the Dollanganger and Casteel series!<br /><br />Heaven is the first book of the Casteel series and even though I enjoyed the Dollanganger series overall more than the Casteel series, Heaven is may favorite of all V.C. Andrews’ books! I liked it even more than Flowers in the Attic, which I never thought possible!<br /><br />Rereading Heaven was an even more amazing than reading it the first time because years later I had read more books and had more books to compare it with! And still… There are no books like V.C. Andrews’! Her books have been translated to nineteen languages and made into twelve film adaptations!<br /><br />I PROMISE THIS IS GOOD STUFF PEOPLE! GOOD STUFF! YOU GOTTA READ THEM!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7188052478989985854" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_247813510" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/247813510" />
    <a title="Heidi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2269664-heidi"><img alt="Heidi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1253592394p2/2269664.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/247813510?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heidi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heidi" href="/user/show/2269664-heidi">Heidi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer247813510" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11329066994278000044">This was a favorite from my early teenage years, so when I saw it on sale, I thought I'd see if the magic was still there. The answer was a resounding NO. Sad.<br/><br/>The first half of the book wasn't so bad. Heaven Leigh Casteel (the name should have been my first clue...) lives in the hills of West Virginia, and her family is at the bottom of the pecking order in their small town. Actually, the Casteels live out of town, up in the hills. (Seven miles away from town, to be exact. Yet it only takes them</span>
  <span id="freeText11329066994278000044" style="display:none">This was a favorite from my early teenage years, so when I saw it on sale, I thought I'd see if the magic was still there. The answer was a resounding NO. Sad.<br /><br />The first half of the book wasn't so bad. Heaven Leigh Casteel (the name should have been my first clue...) lives in the hills of West Virginia, and her family is at the bottom of the pecking order in their small town. Actually, the Casteels live out of town, up in the hills. (Seven miles away from town, to be exact. Yet it only takes them an hour to walk to and from town for school or church, but if Grandpa is with them it can take them them up to two hours. Quite the speed-walking family.) She cares for her younger brothers and sisters with her hard-working but increasingly depressed stepmother, while her father is largely absent. So far, so good. Heaven is a bit of a wuss, and the conversation is stilted, but there's not much to complain about.<br /><br />Halfway through the book, Heaven's father sells all his children to childless couples, for $500 each. In her new wealthy household with a new stepmother and stepfather, Heaven turns into a complainer: she has to wear K-Mart clothes (which aren't good enough for her fashion tastes, even though she had only rags to wear before), she has to do chores around the house (this sort of whining probably appealed to me as a teenager), and her new stepmother doesn't love her enough. <br /><br />Oh, and when her stepmother is in the hospital, Heaven seduces her stepfather and then feels terrible about it. Um, gross?<br /><br />From what I remember, the series keeps getting worse, with worse and worse things happening to Heaven, who never learns to stick up for herself. So I won't be reading onward.<br /><br />(Side note: I think V.C. Andrews is the only author I know of who has written more books after dying than she wrote when she was alive. Seems kind of unfair to other authors, whose careers stop at death.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="11329066994278000044" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66639925-amber-j?shelf=2019-reading-challenge">2019-reading-challenge</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3037072095" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18394066973376609361"><b>
  <i>“If you work to obtain your goal, and realize from the very beginning that nothing valuable comes easily, and still forge ahead, without a doubt you’ll reach your goal, whatever it is.”<br/>― V.C. Andrews, Heaven</i>
</b><br/><br/><i>I try to express only my most honest opinion in a spoiler free way. If you feel anything in my review is a spoiler and is not already hidden in spoiler brackets please let me know. Thank you.</i><br/><p>Heaven lives in a small little house on a mountain in West Virginia. She has an older brother a yo</p></span>
  <span id="freeText18394066973376609361" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>“If you work to obtain your goal, and realize from the very beginning that nothing valuable comes easily, and still forge ahead, without a doubt you’ll reach your goal, whatever it is.”<br />― V.C. Andrews, Heaven</i>
</b><br /><br /><i>I try to express only my most honest opinion in a spoiler free way. If you feel anything in my review is a spoiler and is not already hidden in spoiler brackets please let me know. Thank you.</i><br /><p>Heaven lives in a small little house on a mountain in West Virginia. She has an older brother a younger brother, and two younger sisters. Things aren't easy for them. They are very poor and their dad isn't around much, usually out drinking or bedding what little money they have. Its hard work and a hard life for Heaven but she loves the mountains. Things are changing for Heaven though and they are changing fast and not all of it is good. (Sorry for the vague blurb. I don't know what else to say without giving away any spoilers.)</p><br /><p>So ever since I was able to read a book this size, I have loved V.C. Andrews. I knew even then that the books were a bit preverted and there seems to always be a little bit incest like things happening, but still the stories are intriguing and always pretty dark. This one was no exception to any of that. As a child/teen when I read this book. I felt bad for Heaven, but loved the adventure that was happening. As an adult I just hate all the adults in this story. ALL of them are messed up, I swear. Anyways, I will continue on with the series eventually.</p><br /><p>
  <i>How I choose my rating:<br />1* Did not finish, or hated it but forced myself to finish.<br />2** Didn't really like it. Didn't hate it but not sure why I finished it other then for some closure.<br />3*** I liked it. I had some issues with it, but as a whole it was good. I probably won't reread again ever, but there is a chance I might finish the series. (If part of one) But if not it's not a huge loss.<br />4**** I really liked this book. Maybe not a work of genius, but highly entertaining. I might reread this again, and I will finish the series. (If part of one) I would recommend to those I know hold interest in this books content.<br />5***** I loved this book. I found little to no issues with it at all. I will definitely be rereading this and probably more than once. I will finish the series and reread it multiple times. (If part of one) I will recommend this book to EVERYONE!!!!</i>

<div id="review_677985691" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/677985691" />
    <a title="Zoe&#39;s Human" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17061542-zoe-s-human"><img alt="Zoe&#39;s Human" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1526828338p2/17061542.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/677985691?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zoe&#39;s Human" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zoe&#39;s Human" href="/user/show/17061542-zoe-s-human">Zoe&#39;s Human</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/4546370-heaven">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17061542-zoe-s-human?shelf=lt">lt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17061542-zoe-s-human?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer677985691" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9423087238054661665">This year, I decided to do a 12-book reading challenge. Or, if I'm being more accurate, I decided to buy the Book Riot Read Harder Challenge book log because it was beautiful, and it contained a challenge, so I'm doing it.<br/><br/>Anyway ... Challenge #2 is "Read a book you would normally consider a guilty pleasure". This was a problem for me. I don't have guilty pleasures. Philosophically speaking, I don't even believe in the concept except as a manifestation of the many things wrong with our society. I</span>
  <span id="freeText9423087238054661665" style="display:none">This year, I decided to do a 12-book reading challenge. Or, if I'm being more accurate, I decided to buy the Book Riot Read Harder Challenge book log because it was beautiful, and it contained a challenge, so I'm doing it.<br /><br />Anyway ... Challenge #2 is "Read a book you would normally consider a guilty pleasure". This was a problem for me. I don't have guilty pleasures. Philosophically speaking, I don't even believe in the concept except as a manifestation of the many things wrong with our society. If what you're doing isn't harmful to another and you enjoy it, it is simply a pleasure. I'm not embarrassed by the things I love. <br /><br />After some thought, I concluded that the closest I could get to this would be to pick up a book that I had loved in my early teens. Given how much I've changed over the course of a few decades, I was bound to find something to be embarrassed about in a book I loved then. If nothing from your teens gives you cause to blush as an adult, you probably didn't do it right. I settled on <u>Heaven</u> by V.C. Andrews, because I read it when it came out. I was 13, and, oh, how I loved V.C. Andrews. How I loved this book in particular. I tore through all of the books she had written and was genuinely upset when she died in 1986. <br /><br />I thought I might feel mildly embarrassed to have loved such a soap opera as a teen. I suspected the writing might not be that great. I vaguely hoped that I would find it to be good, that I would learn that even if my taste had been somewhat more salacious at that age that I still would find some familiar seed of quality in the book. What I have found is so much worse than I expected.<br /><br />These books are absolute trash. Racist, classist, slut-shaming stereotypical garbage all mixed in with every trope ever to have come out of the unhappy mind of a properly angsty pubescent teen girl and strung together into a borderline magnificently bad story. <br /><br />I DNFed this book at page 58. I'm not sure how most folks feel about DNFing a challenge book, but it's my challenge, and I choose to save my sanity rather than finish this appalling rubbish.<br /><br />Last, and most importantly, I am grateful not to be the girl who adored this book anymore. This aborted reread has utterly validated my belief that human beings are capable of deep and genuine change.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9423087238054661665" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2760614260" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2760614260" />
    <a title="Corinne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5790525-corinne"><img alt="Corinne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516980145p2/5790525.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2760614260?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Corinne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Corinne" href="/user/show/5790525-corinne">Corinne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5790525-corinne?shelf=for-the-podcast">for-the-podcast</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5790525-corinne?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5790525-corinne?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5790525-corinne?shelf=bonkers">bonkers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2760614260" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2930722055991382543"><b>We read <i>Heaven</i> by VC Andrews for Episode 45 of <a href='https://thebookstorepodcast.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Bookstore</a>. You can listen to it wherever you get your podcasts.</b><br/><br/>It's really a shame that we lost VC Andrews so soon after she began getting published. I'd really love to have a few more interviews with her about her life. She's been central to the identity of so many young readers, that some times I can't believe we ever talk about anything else.<br/><br/>Heaven is a teen girl, the oldest sister of the Casteel family; known in their small mountain town for</span>
  <span id="freeText2930722055991382543" style="display:none"><b>We read <i>Heaven</i> by VC Andrews for Episode 45 of <a href="https://thebookstorepodcast.com" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bookstore</a>. You can listen to it wherever you get your podcasts.</b><br /><br />It's really a shame that we lost VC Andrews so soon after she began getting published. I'd really love to have a few more interviews with her about her life. She's been central to the identity of so many young readers, that some times I can't believe we ever talk about anything else.<br /><br />Heaven is a teen girl, the oldest sister of the Casteel family; known in their small mountain town for being poorer than poor social outcasts. Aside from this aspect of class struggle, it hits many of the VC Andrews points that you've come to know and love (love is a very, <i>very</i> bad word for this):<br />1. An obsession with youth<br />2. An emotionally unavailable mother<br />3. An impossibly handsome, but abusive father<br />4. Incest-y tones<br />5. A traumatic bath<br />6. Lolita-like siblings<br />7. The only trustworthy adult is also an idiot who disappears right when you need them the most<br />8. Sexual encounters that are definitely actually rape<br /><br />Of course, the spaces between these occurrences tend to be long, drawn out, boring sections that are also very confused about the timeline because, I'm actually convinced that VC Andrews wrote these books from first page to last without any planning or editing. I don't think <i>Heaven</i> handles any of these themes in a way that is more interesting or excitingly than <i>Flowers in the Attic</i> or <i>My Sweet Audrina</i>, but if you're a completist or looking for a wild read, or just want to read about a teacher who insists his student take a pregnant hamster home for the weekend that her step-mother will not allow in the house, but he really needs Heaven to do it because he's going on vacation and he's taught Heaven how to use a camcorder and he needs her to film the hamster's labor to share the miracle of childbirth with his class, then this is your book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2930722055991382543" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_208507934" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/208507934" />
    <a title="Creepypasta  &amp; Squirrels " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/377753-creepypasta-squirrels"><img alt="Creepypasta  &amp; Squirrels " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481259528p2/377753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/208507934?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Creepypasta  &amp; Squirrels " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Creepypasta  &amp; Squirrels " href="/user/show/377753-creepypasta-squirrels">Creepypasta  &amp; Squirrels </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/377753-creepypasta-squirrels?shelf=favourite-books">favourite-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/377753-creepypasta-squirrels?shelf=most-engaging-stories">most-engaging-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/377753-creepypasta-squirrels?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/377753-creepypasta-squirrels?shelf=not-to-be-missed-series">not-to-be-missed-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer208507934" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5111450989240381027">The only reason I put this on my "Best Books" shelf is for the sentimental value that this book has. This is the very first V.C. Andrews book I ever read, which was a gift from my mother who gave it to me after I got home from school one afternoon. She only said one thing about the book before handing it over; "That poor girl." Which, of course, piqued my curiosity at once. I remember getting in trouble for staying up past my bedtime to continue reading in secret when my mother went back out to </span>
  <span id="freeText5111450989240381027" style="display:none">The only reason I put this on my "Best Books" shelf is for the sentimental value that this book has. This is the very first V.C. Andrews book I ever read, which was a gift from my mother who gave it to me after I got home from school one afternoon. She only said one thing about the book before handing it over; "That poor girl." Which, of course, piqued my curiosity at once. I remember getting in trouble for staying up past my bedtime to continue reading in secret when my mother went back out to the livingroom. "Heaven" was the first in a long series of V.C. Andrews books I couldn't wait to get my hands on and once in my hot little hands devoured like Pringles chips; fully aware that I couldn't read just one book! V.C. Andrews was one of the very rare authors who could fully pull a reader into the story. When I read "Heaven" for the very first time I remember looking up from several chapters to realize that I was so engrossed in the story that three hours had gone by like three seconds and I didn't even notice. That's the thing I always loved about V.C. Andrews' books; while the main character was telling the story, it almost felt like it was actually you in the story and I don't mean it the way first-person narratives try to make you feel in some of today's books. In a V.C. Andrews book it was different. "Heaven" was the book, like many preteens, that opened me up to the joys and wonders of reading. Though, it is embarrassing to admit that I actually cried very hard during the children-for-sale scene. Upon re-reading that scene, and in fact the entire book, I realize how cheesy it was was. But, for all it's cheese it still holds sentimental value for me. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5111450989240381027" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/578430867?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca Coulby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca Coulby" href="/user/show/7407318-rebecca-coulby">Rebecca Coulby</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer578430867" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17457073671428952099">I read this book when I was 14 years old and I fell in love with it. Heaven was a wonderful passionate heroine because she rose above so many obstacles what I liked about her was she reminded me so much of myself she was shy,beautiful,smart,passionate,and courageous. I really liked the romantic aspect of it Logan was the knight in shining armor that saw something that nobody else did what made it even more passionate was the rivalry between her and her sister fanny. Kitty's character in the book</span>
  <span id="freeText17457073671428952099" style="display:none">I read this book when I was 14 years old and I fell in love with it. Heaven was a wonderful passionate heroine because she rose above so many obstacles what I liked about her was she reminded me so much of myself she was shy,beautiful,smart,passionate,and courageous. I really liked the romantic aspect of it Logan was the knight in shining armor that saw something that nobody else did what made it even more passionate was the rivalry between her and her sister fanny. Kitty's character in the book was unbelievably evil and ignorant it was disgraceful the way she treated heaven she didn't want a daughter she wanted a slave. More than anything heaven wanted love and the warmth of a family what made me feel sorry for her was she always tried to please those around her because she wanted to be loved and to be accepted. This was really about the story of a girl who was trying to find out who she really is. What I loved about v.c. Andrews books was they were about feminine heroines who were trying to rise above circumstance and these were strong empowered women that I've come to treasure. The overall message of v.c. Andrews books was what doesn't kill you makes you stronger.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17457073671428952099" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2860789095" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1017521393081824592">I originally read this back in middle school and for whatever reason I remember enjoying it in an ironic way. VC Andrew's writing has been called campy and melodramatic enough that it might have tainted my original point of view. Having read it almost fifteen years later, I am struck by how disturbing and haunting the story of Heaven's survival really is. There was actually one night that Kitty's antics left me so angry I had trouble sleeping. <br/><br/>This wasn't a "fun" read but it was page turning. It</span>
  <span id="freeText1017521393081824592" style="display:none">I originally read this back in middle school and for whatever reason I remember enjoying it in an ironic way. VC Andrew's writing has been called campy and melodramatic enough that it might have tainted my original point of view. Having read it almost fifteen years later, I am struck by how disturbing and haunting the story of Heaven's survival really is. There was actually one night that Kitty's antics left me so angry I had trouble sleeping. <br /><br />This wasn't a "fun" read but it was page turning. It wasn't a hopeful or uplifting story, but it did make me care so much for a couple of the Casteels that they felt like real people. Love is only an illusion, lies rule the day, and maybe you really can never go home again - was Andrews a nihilist?? I'm compelled to read the rest of the series but I'm also kind of afraid. I need to go find Jesus now haha</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13781641629214424073">Back when Andrews books were actually being written by Andrews herself, her main characters seen to be stronger thank the one's we find in 'The New Virginia Andrews' books. <br/><br/>Although Heaven does fall into some of the same traps, for example, sleeping with a guy she doesn't really want to. She does have a more fight about her. <br/><br/>Yes she is sold and abused in her new home by her fake mother Kitty, but she does stand up to Kitty a fair few times and she is always raging at her father throughout the bo</span>
  <span id="freeText13781641629214424073" style="display:none">Back when Andrews books were actually being written by Andrews herself, her main characters seen to be stronger thank the one's we find in 'The New Virginia Andrews' books. <br /><br />Although Heaven does fall into some of the same traps, for example, sleeping with a guy she doesn't really want to. She does have a more fight about her. <br /><br />Yes she is sold and abused in her new home by her fake mother Kitty, but she does stand up to Kitty a fair few times and she is always raging at her father throughout the book. <br /><br />Talking of Kitty, I first read this book almost twenty years ago and I haven't been able to take a bath since, without thinking of that scene. Being dunked in a boiling hot bath and scrubbed with disinfectant must have been horrific and I have never been able to get it out of my head. <br /><br />Heaven hasn't had any romantic dealings with her brother yet, although they are very close. I can't remember what happens in the rest of her books, though I have a feeling the incest happens with her uncle and not her brother. <br /><br />Looking forward to re-reading the rest of the series.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer120122153" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8662905965367471208">I read this somewhere around the beginning of middle school, and if I had first read it as an adult it probably wouldn't have been given anywhere near 4 stars. I couldn't bring myself to rate it lower for a couple reasons: I remember <i>absolutely loving</i> the book, and on the "V.C. Andrews" scale of literature, it's probably her most engaging story.<br/><br/>I went on to read what must have been a dozen or more by Andrews during my childhood and adolescence, and I've forgotten the majority of the plot lines f</span>
  <span id="freeText8662905965367471208" style="display:none">I read this somewhere around the beginning of middle school, and if I had first read it as an adult it probably wouldn't have been given anywhere near 4 stars. I couldn't bring myself to rate it lower for a couple reasons: I remember <i>absolutely loving</i> the book, and on the "V.C. Andrews" scale of literature, it's probably her most engaging story.<br /><br />I went on to read what must have been a dozen or more by Andrews during my childhood and adolescence, and I've forgotten the majority of the plot lines from her other books. The other reviewers are largely correct in that it's soap-opera fluff and pure guilty reading, but I'm praising it in purely <i>relative</i> terms. It's less formulaic than the others and even a bit less incest-y.<br /><br />I always had this impression that <i>Flowers In The Attic</i> was on the 'General Public Required Reading List' simply because of its notoriety. I would suggest that if any uninitiated reader wants to read Andrews, they read both that book and this one (and hell, read <i>Ruby</i> too, it wasn't half bad). The rest can be safely skipped.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8662905965367471208" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12558730-m-m-strawberry-library-reviews?shelf=20th-century">20th-century</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer408030206" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5686794892571064746">While I felt that the Flowers in the Attic was a excellent book, I feel that the Casteel series is overall the best (at least, the parts written by VC herself) I have read this book 7 or 8 times, and I never get tired of it. And this book is only the beginning of a excellent series, so if you're looking to spend a good amount of hours reading something wonderful, then start with Heaven!<br/><br/>You can't help but feel bad for this poor girl since she is so mistreated by her father for something that was </span>
  <span id="freeText5686794892571064746" style="display:none">While I felt that the Flowers in the Attic was a excellent book, I feel that the Casteel series is overall the best (at least, the parts written by VC herself) I have read this book 7 or 8 times, and I never get tired of it. And this book is only the beginning of a excellent series, so if you're looking to spend a good amount of hours reading something wonderful, then start with Heaven!<br /><br />You can't help but feel bad for this poor girl since she is so mistreated by her father for something that was not even her fault! You wonder why things happen the way they do, but much like Flowers in the Attic, the story of Heaven continues through a series, and the Heaven series is just as enjoyable, with VCA's writing talent but a different story from Flowers in the Attic so that this series isn't repetitive or boring. Enjoy! </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer38717039" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1593936756357818475">Like many, I became engulfed in the white trash drama of the Casteel family in the seventh grade. Ashley Anderson gave me a copy in Mr. Nelson's science class one day and from that moment on (or at least for the next year or so, until I finished the series), my life was changed. I gave the book five stars, but keep in mind, I read it over fifteen years ago. However, the impact was obviously huge. So take the reccomondation how you see fit. Also-Just for fun....Compare and contrast Heaven by VC A</span>
  <span id="freeText1593936756357818475" style="display:none">Like many, I became engulfed in the white trash drama of the Casteel family in the seventh grade. Ashley Anderson gave me a copy in Mr. Nelson's science class one day and from that moment on (or at least for the next year or so, until I finished the series), my life was changed. I gave the book five stars, but keep in mind, I read it over fifteen years ago. However, the impact was obviously huge. So take the reccomondation how you see fit. Also-Just for fun....Compare and contrast Heaven by VC Andrews to Fancy by Reba McEntyre. I think you will see the coorelation.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zoLasmTQmcALTzp1PL3RRCiSpjqbmWSsJv7ZX5zpx4pf5rL/R9xHt01UrFHU3vL/P+aI3c5CyXPa7dJt32MUXQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('W/7QN+gR+eyap3NU4ejaUdu7JC5bBPXGe3donLz9N+/Kmrh6yx0nm9y85XAJi/nqzM8KyQ7fWBmHZGOu/3fkOA==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17311823792202503623"><b>Books published under the following names - <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/13312974._Virginia_Andrews' title=' Virginia Andrews' rel='nofollow noopener'> Virginia Andrews</a>, V. Andrews, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/14980120._Virginia_C__Andrews' title=' Virginia C. Andrews' rel='nofollow noopener'> Virginia C. Andrews</a> & V.C. Endrius. Books since her death ghost written by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/145370.Andrew_Neiderman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Andrew Neiderman</a>, but still attributed to the V.C. Andrews name</b><br/><br/>Virginia Cleo Andrews (born Cleo Virginia Andrews) was born June 6, 1923 in Portsmouth, Virginia. The youngest child and the only daughter of William Henry Andrews, a career navy man who</span>
  <span id="freeText17311823792202503623" style="display:none"><b>Books published under the following names - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/13312974._Virginia_Andrews" title=" Virginia Andrews" rel="nofollow noopener"> Virginia Andrews</a>, V. Andrews, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/14980120._Virginia_C__Andrews" title=" Virginia C. Andrews" rel="nofollow noopener"> Virginia C. Andrews</a> &amp; V.C. Endrius. Books since her death ghost written by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/145370.Andrew_Neiderman" rel="nofollow noopener">Andrew Neiderman</a>, but still attributed to the V.C. Andrews name</b><br /><br />Virginia Cleo Andrews (born Cleo Virginia Andrews) was born June 6, 1923 in Portsmouth, Virginia. The youngest child and the only daughter of William Henry Andrews, a career navy man who opened a tool-and-die business after retirement, and Lillian Lilnora Parker Andrews, a telephone operator. She spent her happy childhood years in Portsmouth, Virginia, living briefly in Rochester, New York. The Andrews family returned to Portsmouth while Virginia was in high school.<br /><br />While a teenager, Virginia suffered a tragic accident, falling down the stairs at her school and incurred severe back injuries. Arthritis and a failed spinal surgical procedure forced her to spend most of her life on crutches or in a wheelchair.<br /><br />Virginia excelled in school and, at fifteen, won a scholarship for writing a parody of Tennyson's <i>Idylls of the King</i>. She proudly earned her diploma from Woodrow Wilson High School in Portsmouth. After graduation, she nurtured her artistic talent by completing a four-year correspondence art course while living at home with her family.<br /><br />After William Andrews died in the late 1960s, Virginia helped to support herself and her mother through her extremely successful career as a commercial artist, portrait painter, and fashion illustrator.<br /><br />Frustrated with the lack of creative satisfaction that her work provided, Virginia sought creative release through writing, which she did in secret. In 1972, she completed her first novel, <i>The Gods of the Green Mountain</i> [sic], a science-fantasy story. It was never published. Between 1972 and 1979, she wrote nine novels and twenty short stories, of which only one was published. "I Slept with My Uncle on My Wedding Night", a short fiction piece, was published in a pulp confession magazine.<br /><br />Promise gleamed over the horizon for Virginia when she submitted a 290,000-word novel, <i>The Obsessed</i>, to a publishing company. She was told that the story had potential, but needed to be trimmed and spiced up a bit. She drafted a new outline in a single night and added "unspeakable things my mother didn't want me to write about." The ninety-eight-page revision was re-titled <i>Flowers in the Attic</i> and she was paid a $7,500 advance. Her new-generation Gothic novel reached the bestseller lists a mere two weeks after its 1979 paperback publication by Pocket Books.<br /><br /><i>Petals on the Wind</i>, her sequel to <i>Flowers</i>, was published the next year, earning Virginia a $35,000 advance. The second book remained on the New York Times bestseller list for an unbelievable nineteen weeks (<i>Flowers</i> also returned to the list). These first two novels alone sold over seven million copies in only two years. The third novel of the Dollanganger series, <i>If There Be Thorns</i>, was released in 1981, bringing Virginia a $75,000 advance. It reached No. 2 on many bestseller lists within its first two weeks.<br /><br />Taking a break from the chronicles of Chris and Cathy Dollanganger, Virginia published her one, and only, stand-alone novel, <i>My Sweet Audrina</i>, in 1982. The book welcomed an immediate success, topping the sales figures of her previous novels. Two years later, a fourth Dollanganger novel was released, <i>Seeds of Yesterday</i>. According to the New York Times, <i>Seeds</i> was the best-selling fiction paperback novel of 1984. Also in 1984, V.C. Andrews was named "Professional Woman of the Year" by the city of Norfolk, Virginia.<br /><br />Upon Andrews's death in 1986, two final novels—<i>Garden of Shadows</i> and <i>Fallen Hearts</i>—were published. These two novels are considered the last to bear the "V.C. Andrews" name and to be almost completely written by </span>
